90S Broadway, April 15.
"Whereas, A petition has been
flied and is now pending before the
Corns of Kneineers. U. S. A., at
"Whereas, A petition has been
flied and is now pending before the
Corps of Engineers, U. S. A., at
San Francisco, Cal., seeking to
have moved landwards pierhead
lines in the Oakland harbor as es
tablished about five years ago by
the Federal Government, the effect
of which change would be to put
new pierhead lines and all wharves
and landings solely upon land
claimed by t Water Front Com
pany, leaving no free water front
age or landing place under the con
trol of the public as Is now the case
under the decision of the Supreme
Court of the State of California, as
it now stands:
solved. That this body views
proposed change with great
alarm, as against the public inter-
. gainst the growth of Oakland
ami the rig.Â»t of the city and the
whole public; and this body does
most strongly protest against any
change "f pierhead lines, the effect
of whicn would be to limit wharves,
Its, piers or landing places to
territory clal: d in private owner
;i:us taking the dominion and
control of the city front out of the
hands of the public and putting it
in the hands of individuals, or of
a private corporation organized for
profit. And this body protests
against any change of harbor lines
the effect of which would be to
diminish the area of water front
now under public control; and be
it further
"Resolved, That the officers and
directors of this body be and they
are hereby directed to appear at the
hearing of said petition in support
of this resolution and to oppose any
change of pierhead lines."
A special meeting of the Board of Trade
xrns held this morning to consider what
Fteps should be taken relative to the at
tempt to change the pierhead lines along
the water front. This Question to take
the water front controversy out of the
hands of the Supreme Court and to work
through the United States engineer's of
fice is considered to be of primary im
portance-, and at the meeting next Mon
day in San Francisco there will be many
arguments presented on behalf of this
city? interest.
Attorney Lair Hill, who has had a large
Fhare in representing Oakland's side In
the litigation, explained to the directors
how the petition of Brock & Co. to have
the pierhead lines changed would affect
the city's right.
Councilman Pringle, who was present,
paid: "This move is nothing more nor
less than an effort of the Water Front
pany to get around the decision giv
ing us a right to the water front. It will
need an enort on our part to get the en
gineers to decide in our favor. The Board
of Trade should send a delegation Id the
meeting on Monday."
A suggestion having been made in favor
of calling a mass meeting to protest
ne.iinst the import of the petition, the
matter wan discussed, but the board de
. i'led that little was to be gained by such
a general demonstration and that a "strong
protest backed by sound argument before
the United States Engineers would be the
letter plan. The resolution already quot
ed was then passed unanimously.
The Ordinance and Judiciary Committee
or the City Council has decided that it
â will be better to countenance the appear
ance of the special attorneys for the city
at Monday's meeting. The matter was
discussed by the committee last night
and on the representation of Mr. T'pton
:he attorneys are willing to appear
without compensation, it was decided to
Include the words "without compensa
tion" in the resolution and recommend its
adoption. Although this resolution will
not he acted upon by the City Council
until next night, when the con
ference in the engineers' office will have
closed, it is significant inasmuch as it
shows that several o. the Councilmen who
voted against it last Monday night have
been forced by the pressure of public
opinion and general protest to change
their votes. There is no doubt that in
accordance with the spirit 01 the resolu
tion as recommended, the city's attorneys
will be present.

Death of John H. Kercheval in Oak-
land After a Long Illness.
OAKLAND, April 15â The death of
John H. Kercheval, the material agent
of the Southern Pacific Company, at hÂ»s
home in this city last night, has removed
a man well-known throughout the coast.
He comes of a French Huguenot family,
whose original name was Coeur de
Cheval, meaning the "heart of a horse."
Mr. Kercheval was born on Hickory
Farm, near Jollet, 111., September 26, 1836.
and came to this State December 10. 1553.
He returned In the spring and became
deputy sheriff of Will County. Illinois.
He enlisted In Company R. Tenth Illinois
volunteers, at the Hist call of men for
the civil war. but his health compelled
him to give up in about a year, tie re
turned to California in ISG7. began his
career as a railroad man aa brakeman
on the first passenger train over the
summit. He has remained with the com
pany ever since.

POOLROOMS
NOT ILLEGAL
Judge Allen Annuls the
Law Prohibiting
Them.
The Head of the Ordinance Is
Not Harmonious With
the Body.
Nothing to Prevent Open Pool-Sell
ing Now in All the Cigar
*Storea.
Oakland Office San Francisco Call,
908 Broadway, April 15.
When the Supreme Court declared that
the Stratlon primary law was unconsti
tutional because the title and the body
of the act did not agree they made It pos
sible for poolrooms to be at once opened
In Oakland and run without fear of mo
lestation by the police.
This morning Judge Allen declared the
famous anti-poolroom ordinance, which
was passed after the bitterest agitation
ever seen In this city, in 1592, to be In
valid on the ground that the title of the
measure did not correspond with its va
rious sections. As a result of this decis
ion the raid on the pool-sellers made
several weeks ago is without effect, and
D. P. Clark. A. D. Dennis, W. Wolfsohn
and C. McPiale were discharged in the
Police Court and the charges against
them were dismissed.
There is now no bar to the opening of
poolrooms In this city and conducting
them "wide open," unless the City Coun
cil should amend the ordinance and make
its head and tail agree. This is more
than is expected from the "solid six,"
and undoubtedly there will bo a great
anti-poolroom campaign inaugurated at
once.
Attorney T. M. Bradley, who repre
sented the pool-sellers in the Police
Court, moved tor a dismissal on the
ground that the title of the ordinance
under which the arrests were made did
not mention specifically that the receiv
ing of money to bet on races was pro
hiuited, while In the body of the article
such prohibition iÂ« ordained. He says
his client only received money to bet on
races for other parties.
A. A. Moore Jr., representing the Dis
trict Attorney";* oflice, while admitting
that Mr. Bradley's point might be well
tukin, asked for a continuance of a few
days to look the matter up. Attorney
Bradley insisted on an immediate " de
cision, and Judge Allen declared the or
dinance void and discharged the defend
ant.
The title of the ordinance reads: "An
ordinance prohibiting In certain places
within the city of Oakland the selling of
pools or making of beis or wagers on
contest between men or between horses,
wherein money or other articles of value
are staked or played."
In the ordinance Is the following sec
tion, upon which the pool-sellers base
their argument:
No person upon any trial or contest of skill,
speed or power of endurance, between men, or
â  between horseÂ». shall, within the limits of the
city ot Oakland, Bell, issue or dispose of any
ticket, certificate or other evidence of payment,
on which -shall be Inscribed, written marked
or printed any number, name, word, mark or
! device to desiunate the choice selected, received
or accepted by any other person to entitle or
enable the said person holding the ticket, cer
tificate or other evidence of payment to galfc
or lose on any contingent Issue; or receive any
article of value or any money or anything rep
resenting money, or any articule of value, as
a bet, wager or hazard upon the event of any
contest or contingent stake, or an a stake or
pledge between two or more parties or to dis
burse the said money or any portion thereof or
anything representing money ur other article
of value upon any representations or condition
or tn any conformity to or with any express or
tacit understanding or agreement.
When ex-Chief Lloyd made his raid on
the pool-sellers he stated that pool-sell
ing was being conducted on such a vl-
Eplan and In so many places that
ren not over H years of age of both
i were being taught to gamble and
putting up even as low as a dime
on the chances of horses. There Is no
doubt that the moral slue of the question
will receive immediate attention, and
there are many who think that Judge
Allen rendered his decision on a point
smaller than will be recognized should
the case be appealed to a higher court.

HARMONY PREVAILS.
A New Lease of Life for the Young
Men's Republican League.
OAKLAND, April 15.â The Young Men's
Republican League took on a new lease
in its career to-night, and it is now be
lieved that harmony Is assured and that
within a few weeks the league will have
1000 enrolled members. President Breed
opened the proceedings with a very strong
statement of the position of the club with
regard to the two candidates for Gover
nor in this city. "After all that has been
said by unauthorized parties, ir ,'"said the
president. "I feel that a statement Is ab
solutely necessary at this time to place
the club in a truthful position before the
party In Alameda County. I brand as
I false and unauthorized any statement
that declares this league has indorsed or
is working in the interest of any candi
date for any office. This falsehood has
been freely circulated, and although we
have received Tair treatment from the
I press, the rumor has not yet been suffi
ciently exploded. After the convention
we win get behind all the Republican
candidates and work with all our might,
but not until then. Now, it is our pur
pose to build up a strong party organi
zation, loyal to Republicanism, but hot
to individuals striving for nominations."
This declaration was louuly cheered, and
some very kind things were said about
those who belonged to the league two
years ago but who have not yet joined the
ranks. Everything that was said in the
discussion that followed looked to har
mony, and anything that might be con
strued as inimical to those who are sup
posed to be in the Pulcifer camp was
carefully avoided. Charles Hall spoke of
the struggle between the candidates for
Governor, and said that the County Com
mittee should take the matter in hand
and should end the fight. : â¦
Mr. Knowles said that if Alameda did
not soon end her quarrel she would find
that Mr. Flint take the matter had hand
should end the fight,
r. Knowles said that if Alameda did
soon end her quarrel she would find
: Mr. Flint of San Benito had cap
tured the prize. James Oliver of Berke
ley Introduced a resolution commending
the course of President McKinley, and it
was carried unanimously and enthusi
astically. Many other speeches were
i made, and a desire for harmony was the
expression of all. a
At the close of the meeting it was found
that nearly 400 had signed Lie roll. Coffee
and sandwiches were generously pro
vided, and the affair marked a new era of
good feeling in the life of the club It is
now believed that Harry Pulcifer and his
followers will accept the offer of the
league to have representation on the ex
ecutive committee and that all will enroll
The declaration of non-partisanlsm by
I President Breed has paved the way for
speedy union.

SHE SEEKS TO RECOVER.
Mrs. Lenore E. Taylor Sues Her Hus-
band to Collect on a Mainte
nance Contract.
OAKLAND. April 15.â Mrs. Lenore E.
Taylor of Berkeley has filed a suit
against "her husband for $1200, due her
for maintenance, according to the terms
of an agreement entered Into by the par
ties JanuaiV 5, 1897. The parties are
living apart and have for some time, but
the husband has paid $75 per month for
the support of his wife and two chil
dren.
Mr. and Mrs. Taylor were married in
Oarfleld, Colo., October 9, ISB9, and have
two childrenâ Ethel A., aged 14. and
Frederick E., aged 10 years. Owing to
their inability to live together peacea
bly they drew up an agreement to sep
arate, the wife to have the care and
custody of the children. The husband
agreed to pay his wife $50 per month for
maintenance, and Charles A. Bailey, as
trustee, $25 per month, until the Berke
ley home was cleared of debt, and waived
all his rights to the property.
It is alleged In the complaint that he
is now behind $1203, and it is this which
the wife seeks to recover in her suit.
His Heart Failed.
OAKLAND, April 15.â Rev. Father
Nolan of St. Mary's Church was taken
with a very peculiar fainting spell at the
Receiving Hospital while taking the dy
ing confession of G. Fenetia. His body
turned cold and his pulse dropped to 20
beats a minute. Steward Tobin and Dr.
R. S. Stratton took him in charge, and
after an hour's work revived him to con
sciousness. He is now at home resting
easy, and it is believed all danger Is past.
Heart failure is supposed to be the
trouble.

The Reservoir Completed.
BERKELEY, April ]r..-Rf.gent J. F.
Houghton, chairman of the committee on
reservoir, to-day visited the new 300,000
gallon roservoir in Strawberry Canyon,
which has Just been completed.
On Sunday the water from Strawberry
Creek will be turned into the reservoir
by means of the new dam, higher up the
canyon, and It is expected that the reser
voir will be filled in about a week.
Mains have been laid to the various
parts of the university grounds, and En
gineer Boardman believes that in addi
tion to furnishing an adequate supply in
case of fire, the new reservoir will make
it possible tn sprinkle the roadways and
irrigate the gardens of the college
grounds throughout the summer.

last evening at the parsonage.
It has been proved, as the result of ex
periments, that tho circulation of the
blood is affected by music.
ASTON SAYS HE
WAS A FRIEND
Only Visited Mrs. Rojas
to Pay for Work
Done.
Denies the Allegation That He
Was Caught Kissing
the Lady.
Alvarado's Dlvorco Cnso May Be
tho Cause of a Lively-
Trial.
Oakland Office San Francisco Call,
908 Broadway, April 15.
"When the divorce case of the Rojases
comes up in Judge Hall's courtroom there
will probably be a lively trial. Philip H.
Aston, whose name appears in the com
plaint, says that only one side of the
story has yet been told. The case has
excited much interest in Alvarado, where
the parties live, and has been a fruitful
theme for gossip for several months, both
parties to the controversy apparently
having many friends.
"I have been brought into this case on
false representations," Bald Mr. Aston.
"The facts are as follows: Rojas deserted
his wife on September 3 of last year, after
he beat and abused uer most shamefully.
Mrs. Rojas was at that time in destitute
circumstances, and, in fact, had not the
necessaries of life. On the day mentioned
Mrs. Rojas had him arrested for battery,
to which charge he pleaded guilty and
paid his fine. The poor lady came to me
in her great trouble for assistance, and
askeu me to give her my washing to
help her to sustaJn life for her three
children. I gave her work, and never
visited her till December 13, when I went
to her house about half-past 8 In the
evening to pay her. We were sitting in
the kitchen and talking together, when
Mr. Rojas rushed in and accused me of
kissing his wife, and abused her shame
fully. After considerable talking I left
for my home. I again yisited Mrs. Rojas
on December 17 to get a vest which I had
sent her that day for repairs. Rojas
again entered the house and raised a dis
turbance, but there was no fighting or
thrashing at these times. One night in
February ho waylaid me in the dark and
hit me unawares on the head, in a public
street, for which I had him arrested. Mrs.
Rojas is highly respected by all the good
people of this town, ajid they are now
helping her by giving her work; but I
cannot say the same for Mr. Rojas. When
the case comes up before Judge HaJl on
April 25 tne rest of this story will be
made public-^

GUARDIAN IN TROUBLE.
Gave Possession of Property Before
Authorized by the Court.
OAKLAND, April 15.â The guardian of
Mary Peterman, an incompetent, has
placed himself in a peculiar predicament.
Last Monday the sale of certain prop
erty was up for comf.rmation by the
court. One of the family had bid $2000,
but this was run up to $2425 by an out
sider. The court found the bidder had
no coin up. so refused to make the or
der until $500 was produced, and continued
the case until evening, then until Tues
day and finally until to-day, as no cash
came into court.
The bidder, however, who resides near
the guardian, at Haywards. paid the full
price Monday afternoon, and was given
possession. When the case was called
to-day a new bid of $2500 was offered.
The guardian's attorney objected and
made the explanation given here, but the
court refused to allow it, and confirmed
the new bid. The next move is awaited
with interest, as the court said the par
ties in possession had no title, the guard
lan having no authority to act without
the court's order..

There was a clergyman in a Long Island village who suf-
fered from dyspepsia to such an extent that it positively seemed
sometimes as though his doctrine was not sound. It was, however,
only a stomach trouble, and had nothing to do with the mind.
Being convinced of this, one of his parishioners, a lady, presented
him with a small quantity of Ripans Tabules and the relief he ex-
perienced was such that all the congregation noticed an improve-
ment, and now, although his salary is small, this clergyman and
his wife devote a portion of it to keeping the medicine closet
stocked with a suitable supply of Ripans Tabules. Doubtless
there are many cases where what has been thought heresy was in
fact nothing more nor less than dyspepsia, and Ripans Tabules euro
dyspepsia. One gives relief.

LYNN PUZZLES
THE DOCTORS
A Little Ruse That Shows He
Has Intervals of Common
Sense.
Experts Disagree in Court and More.
Are Sent For to Unravel
the Tangle.
Oakland Office San Francisco Call,
90S Broadway, April 18.
J. W. Lynn is causing the doctors and
officials and an army of witnesses a
great deal of trouble. Some declare he
is Insane, others declare he Is not, and
several are doubtful. For three hours
this afternoon Lynn was before Judge
Ogden while a judicial examination was
conducted as to his sanity.
As he was being conducted from the
insane ward to the courtroom a little in
cident occurred that tended to shake the
faith of some in Lynn's insanity. The
Chief of Police had planned a little ruse
that worked to his entire satisfaction.
He had several officers present and as
Lynn was going up the steps the Chief
said: "If this man jroes off Into one of
those struggling fits, just beat him haif
to death: don't waste any strength
wrestling with him."
This order seemed to have the effect
of renderlnir Lynn very sane, for he
turned to Chief Fletcher and said very
rationally, "If that's the way you are
going to treat me. I won't go." Ordi
narily .Lynn does not notice any conver
sation.
The case has now reached the interest
ing stage where doctors disagree.
"Lynn is crazy," swear Drs. Rabe and
"Lynn is sane." swear Drs. Rucker and
J. P. Dunn. And the court is in doubt.
After examining many witnesses, it
was decided to send for Dr. Hatch of
Sacramento and the physicians at Ag
news, where Lynn was employed, all of
whom will testify as experts. The casÂ«
was continued until to-morrow morning.
This is the most protracted insanity trial
ever held in this county, and bids fair to
be the most expensive.

times more productive than potatoes and
123 times more than wheat.

MORE TROUBLE
FOR GOLD BUG
The Short-Legged Run
ner Won a Dash and
Caused Commotion.
The Talent Confronted With
Perplexing Problems at
Oakland.
Ojat Downed a Field of Youngster*.
Rubicon Caused Trouble for
th<s Books.
There was one race declfled at Oak
land yesterday, that caused considera
ble confusion. It was the opening
live and a half furlong scramble, the
"doggiest" event of the card. Gold
Bug won, and whenever the short
legged sprinter scores there is always
trouble brewing. The last time out
Gus Wilson rode him, and he showed
nothing. Yesterday the ex-hurdle rider,
Bob Cairns, had the mount, and at one
time the ring laid 15 to 1 about him.
Just before the horses were called to
the post, a colored trainer by the name
of Lee attempted to give the horse a
"shot," but was caught with the goods
on, and later was ruled off. At any
rate. Gold Buy was played down to
sevens, and In a drive beat Tom Smith
a length. Then the purse was pro
tested on the ground that the winner
was not eligible to start, having won
a race at Kanta Ana some time last
fall. While th^ officials were racking
their brains over the muddle, those in
on the know were cashing their tickets.
The racing throughout was most or
dinary, of the favorites served up but
two were successful in taking purses.
The season Is drawinp to a close and
lirst choices are a dangerous propo
sition.
In the four-furlonK gallnp for two
year-olds OJai. against which 7 to 1 was
once obtainable, out footed his field,
winning easily from Canace. Sweet
Cakes the favorite, was third.
The Blx-furlong sellfn<r sprint next de
cided resulted in a handy win for Va
lencienne. The St. Carlo filly was sec
ond choice in the hotting to Good
Friend, and taking the front position
In the stretch won ridden out from the
favorite. uffK-ial was a good third.
The mile and a sixteenth run was a
windfall for Paul Pry. The ring laid
6 to 5 against the chestnut horse and
he won easily from Robair, corning on
from fourth position. In a hard drive
the 40 i. i shot Metaire secured show
honors filhm Twinkle Twink.
The wise play sent Rubicon to the
post favorite for the second six-fur
lon; run. Mr-Light opened favorite,
but did not receive the caucus nomi
nation, receding to twos. Rubicon led
Throughout, and driving at the finish
got the verdict over Oddson a neck.
McLisrht, away from the post poorly,
v. as third.
The final mile selling run went to
Th"lma. Burko's mare sot all the best
of the start, and backed from 6 to 1
down to 7 to 2, was never headed, lead
ing out the 7 to 5 favorite, Refugee, by
four lengths.

A CONSUL IS
CAUGHT BY CUPID
A. K. Coney Will To-Night
Wed Miss Margaret
Falvey.
Consul-General A. K. Coney of Mexico
to this city will be married this evening
to Miss Margaret G. Falvey, the daugh
ter of Mrs. Mary Falvey of New Bruns
wick. The ceremony, which will be
strictly private, owing to the ill-health
of Consul Coney's mother, will be per
formed by Rev. Father William P. Kirby,
at the home of the groom. The happy
couple will leave on Monday for Los An
geles, and will spend their honeymoon In
the southern part of the State, whir*
they will remain two weeks.
The wedding is the culmination of a
little romance. Miss Falvey having come
to this coast merely on a visit to the Con
sul's mother. Owing to Mrs. Coney's ill
ness, the visit lengthened and Mr. Coney
was so charmed by the tender solicitude
evinced by the fair visitor for her sick
hostess that before he vvaÂ« aware he was
caught irretrievably in Cupid's meshes.
His many friends here will be eager to
extend wannest congratulations to him
self and bride.
Accused Prisoners Acquitted.
Emll Hollerway and Edward Klrby,
boys who were accused of breaking Into
an oyster stand at 29 Third street, were
acquitted yesterday by a Jury In Judge
Cook's court.
Bruno Meyer, who was accused of
having stolen a watch and chain from
Edward A. Muller on January 30 last,
was acquitted yesterday in Judge Bor
den's court.
THE SAN FRANCISCO CALL, SATURDAY, APRIL 1(5, 1898.
THE STOCK MARKET.
Business In mining stocks was dull yesterday
and prices shaded off all around.
The Utah and Gould and Curry assessments ,
fall delinquent in board to-day.
A quarterly dividend of $1 50 per share was :
yesterday paid by the California Safe Deposit
and Trust Company.
The Anaconda Copper Mining Company of '
Montana has declared a dividend of $1 25 per '
share, amounting to $150,000. payable May 2.
The total dividends declared by this company (
to date are $5,400,000.
The Alaska-Treadwell Gold Mining Company
reported for March a total of 21.493 tons of
ore milled. The total bullion yield was $33,290,
an average of $1 55 per ton. Of the bullion >
returned a total of $22,620 came from 348 tons I
of Eulphurets (concentrates) treated by chlor- ;
Inatlon. â¢" ,
The annual meeting of the stockholders of |
the Geary Street. Park and Ocean Railroad
Company, which was to have been held April j
13, has been postponed for one week.
The Highland Mining Company of South Da- \
kato has declared a dividend of 20 cents per .
share, or $20,000, payable on the 19th. This is
the first dividend since October. 1897.
The New York and Honduras Rosarlo Mm- !
ing Company paid a dividend of $15,000 yester- j
day, the third of like amount paid this year. j
This makes a total of $&00,000.
The old directors and officers of the Italian-
Swiss Mutual Loan Association have been re
elected, as follows: President. P. Barbieri; j
vice-president. Dr. Joseph Pescia: treasurer, A. i
Merle: secretary, A. Sbarboro; attorney, D. i
Freidenrich, and P. C. Rossi, Charles A. Maim, j
G. B. Cevasco, D. Paronl and G. de Luca, also
directors.
The Gwin Development and Mining Company
has re-elected the old directors, with M. W.
BelFhaw as president. E. C. . Voorhees vice- i
president. J. J. Crawford secretary and F. F.
Thomas superintendent. During the year Just
closed the amount of ore worked was 48, ISO
tons, the net return on which was $168,823 79 ,
In bullion and. $39,963 35 In sulphurets, a total ;
of $207,963 H. â¢
The Pacific Surety Company is now. paying
a quarterly dividend of 2 per cent.
Business on the Bond Exchange was light ;
again at about the same prices.

CHURCH NOTICES.
THE Evangelist of the Catholic Apostolic
Church. Mr. Davenport, will lecture in Na-
tive Sons' Hall, next Sunday night. Admis-
sion free and no collection. He will speak
of the present condition of the churches,
taking for his text the slumbering ten vir-
gins of the â , parable, and will point to the
rich promises made to "him that overcom-
eth." There Is a church of this kind In this
city, and Its special teachings will be ex-
plained. All are welcome.

TRACED ACROSS THE CONTINENT.
A Real Life Melodrama That Ends
To-Day in the Happy Reunion
of Husband and Wife.

court of the Palace Hotel there will
be enacted to-day the closing scÂ»nÂ» in
a real-life melodrama, the principal
character of which is a young, hand
some and wealthy woman, the daughter

SUMNER RUSH HOLLANDER.
The son of a wealthy Boston merchant, who has twice, during the first year of
his married iife, had his wife torn from his arms and has twice regained her after
spending a fortune in the search that has extended from ocean to ocean.
half a continent; has doggedly pursued
the quest from ocean to ocean and has
expended a fortune in the hire of the
best detectives In the land to continue
the search that ended two days igo
at a tumble-down farm house on a
wind-swept ranch in the foothills of
Glenn County.
Such is a brief outline of a tragic ro
mance in real life that has no equal in
the works of modern fiction.

v/cncVrful succession of even f s is, or
rather was. Miss F. G. Clark. Sho is

own right to a fortune of a quarter of

believed thin munificent bequest, dic
tated by paternal love, is the chief fac
tor in the Borrow and danger that has

tiful bride 1b the final Incident In a
series of events sufficiently strange and
thrilling to touch the most hardened
heart. All doubts and uncertainties
will be for the moment blotted out by
thiÃ happy reunion amongr strangers,
In a strange city, thoue-.i'ids of miles
from home and friends.
Scarcely more than a year ago Sum
ner Hollander, then a young college Btu
dent, and Miss Clark, who was one of
the petted belles of Cambridge society,
met and fell in love with each other.
With the impulsiveness of youth they
decided upon an elopement and
secret marriage rather than be
subjected to the delay incident
to the formality of securing pa
rental consent to their uninn. To
conceive was to act, and with happy
disregard for future consequences the
young couple repaired to a near-by vil
lage and were married by a minister
who was sufficiently discreet not to ask
unpleasant questions.
For three months the marriage was
kept a profound secret, then the young
couple braved parental wrath and gave
their secret to the world. Having re
ceived the forgiveness of their parents
and the congratulations of their friends
the happy husband and wife settled
down to the enjoyment of a life un
shadowed by any warning of future
sorrow. Fpr three weeks they lived
', in happy contentment. Then came the
death of the bride's father, Alvan G.
Clark, an event that was heralded in
the press of two continents. This oc
curred on June 9, 1897, a date that
marked the turning point in the cur
rent of two lives. Since that time hap
piness has been a stranger to the Hol
lander household.
Alvan Clark died a wealthy man.
When his will was read it was found
that he had made a small bequest to
one of his two older daughters. The
other he disinherited. To Mrs. Hollan
der, his youngest and favorite daugh
ter, he bequeathed $20,000 outright, be
sides the sum of $200,000 to be held in
trust for her for a period of ten years,
at the expiration of which period the
money was to be hers unconditionally.
By a provision of the will it was stipu
lated that if Mrs. Hollander died with
out issue before the expiration of the
ten-year period the money was to re
vert to the two remaining sisters, share
and share alike.
It is claimed by both Mr. and Mrs.
Hollander that as soon as the provis
ions of the will became known the two
elder sisters, both of whom are married,
manifested a deep and absorbing intor
est in the welfare of Mrs. Hollander.
The husband and wife go still further
than this and charge the two older sis
ters and their husbands with being di
rectly responsible for all that has since
occurred in the succession of startling,
almost tragic, events now to be so hap
pily terminated.
As already stated these events began
with the death of Alvin Clark and the
reading of his will. At this time Mrs.
Hollander was happy In the hope that
before the end of the year she would
present her husband with a living
pledge of her love and devotion, and
an heir to the fortune willed to her In
trust by her father. This hope was
blasted by means that may only be
hinted at here.
For weeks the young wife's life was
despaired of, and it was only by the
most careful nursing and the atten
tion of the most skilled physicians that
she was dragged back to life from the
brink of the grave. Then one day be
fore Mrs. Hollander had yet recovered
her health and strength her husband
returned home to find that his
wife had disappeared, leaving no trace
behind. From the homes of friende
and acquaintances the search for her
was extended to surrounding towns
and cities, but all to no purpose. The
young wife had disappeared as com
pletely as If the earth had swallowed
her.
Her . husband, crazed with ; grief and
anxiety, {was not .to be comforted. 'His
father, whose . heart â  had , been won Iby
the young wife's charming : personality
agd who, spoked upon her Â»<| ogo of hj^
own children, placed his fortune at the
disposal of his eon In pursuing the
search for the missing wife. The best
detectives in Boston and New York
were employed to aid in the quest, they
being ordered to proceed with the ut
most secrecy and discretion.
After weary weeks of suspense, of
> unfruitful clews and false alarms came
news that gladdened tho hearts of the
young husband and the members of his
family. The wifo had been found. She
had been found, but not as had been
' supposed, in Borne place of involuntary
' detention in one of the great cities of
! the East, but in a lonely farm house
1 that forma a minute dot on the llmit
! less expanse of the prairies of North
Dnkota, far from the haunts of civ
! lllzatlon.
Three days after this intelligence was
i flashed over the wires to the home in
j Boston husband and wife were clasped
lin each other's arms in the dingy
i living room of the weather-beaten
I farmhouse, the detectives standing
| guard to see that no unfriendly hand
or voice marred the momentary hap
piness of the reunion. The explana
tions that followed will be told fur-
ther along in the words of Mr. Hollan
der himself.
A happy home coming followed this
Joyous meeting on the bleak reaches of
the Dakota prairie. Then came a brief
period of comparative tranquillity that
was marred only by the thought that
the young wife might in some way be
made to suffer again by the people
who were held to be responsible for
what had gone before.
Three months passed and the young
wife was again made happy by
the hope of approaching maternity.
Again were these hopes dashed to the
ground by the same agency that had
before robbed her of her desire to be
come a mother. Again was her life
despaired of and again did the skill of
the physicians triumph. A long period
of convalescence followed, and Mr.
Hollander, made happy by the thought
that his wife had been restored to him,
and that death had for a second time
been robbed of a victim, resumed his
business occupations.
On the second day of last month Mr.
Hollander was called away from home
for forty-eight hours on a business
trip. When he returned he found his
wife gone and his home deserted. As
before, no trace of her whereabouts
had been left behind, no note of explan
ation and no message to relieve the
agonizing uncertainty as to what fate
had overtaken the missing woman.
Acting upon the knowledge gained by j
former experience Mr. Hollander called j
in the services of detectives and set
about a systematic search that was
destined to meet with success. After ;
several weeks a clew was found and j
the missing wife was trailed across the I
continent to California- The detectives |
found Mrs. Hollander at a ranch house !
owned by a family named Nye in the
foothills of Glenn County, fourteen
miles from the little town of Willows.
The telegraph conveyed this informa
tion to the anxious husband, who at
once started for the Pacific Coast as I
fast as steam could carry- him. He was ;
accompanied by his attorney, Walter |
S. Sherman. They went direct to Wil- j
lows, where they hired a team and
drove to the ranch house. There dis
appointment awaited them. It appears
that notice of their coming had been j
telegraphed from Boston by spies who
had been detailed to watch the move- |
ments of the husband. This warning
had been given in time to enable those ;
who were seeking to keep Mrs. HOI- ;
lander from her husband to take her ;
from the farm house to another hiding
place.
Disappointed and almost disheart
ened, Mr. Hollander and his attorney
came on to this city and took up their
residence at the Palace Hotel. They
reached Willows April 7 and found
that Mrs. Hollander had been taken
away from the ranch on April 5. They
reached this city April 8. Arriving
here there was nothing left for them to
do but to await the time when the new
hiding-place of :he unhappy wife
should be discovered. This was ac
complished last Thursday afternoon.
Precautions necessary to prevent a re
currence of the defeat and disappoint
ment that was met with upon the ar
rival of the rescuing party at Willows
caused a delay of 36 hours before Mr.
Hollander was notified that the time
had arrived when he could greet the
wife who had been so cruelly separated
from him for a period of almost two
months. Not until this meeting takes
place to-day will they feel themselves
free for a time at least from the dan
gers that seem to surround them.
"This Is the second attempt that has
been made to take my wife from me by
force and violence," said Mr. Holland
er yesterday, "and if there is any law
or Justice in the land It shall be the
last. Both attempts were so nearly
successful that I shudder to think of
the fate that would probably have
overtaken the dear little woman had
it not been my good fortune to find
and rescue her.
"Even to me, who have undergone
tortures of body and mind sufficiently
terrible to make me alive to the real
ity of what has happened, the whole
thing seems like a horrible dream or
the fancy of a diseased mind. It does
not seem possible that in this enlight
ened age there are people who would
not hesitate to do what has been done
to me and mine for the purpose of ac
quiring possession of a few paltry dol
lars.
"Think of it. A woman twice stolen
and taken thousands of miles away and
placed in an obscure hiding place;
twice" subjected to physical treatment
that all but ended in death and result
ed in the sacrifice of two innocent lives.
It is terrible, wrong and inhuman, yet
I doubt if it be possible to bring about
the punishment of the persons I know
to be guilty of these brutal and crim
inal acts. I do not know what to do or
where to turn. It seems that lam una
ble to protect my own wife from those
who would be benefited by any evil
that might be done her.
"The first time; she was taken away
from me I almost lost, my reason, be
cause I was afraid * that j she had been
murdered and her body either concealed
or destroyed. After: weeks of the

A NEW HOME FOR DEPENDENT BOYS.
Youths' Directori] Will Be Open to Unfortunates of All Creeds.
VIEW OF THE NEW YOUTHS' DIRECTORY.
Contracts for the new Youths' Directory to replace the building on Howard street have been signed and re
corded. The institution will be handsome and imposing, and its doors will be open to all creeds. It will cost a
good, round sum, most of which the Rev. F. Crowley expects to raise among the numerous friend 3of this de
serving work.
The reverend director has a new scheme for raising funds, and it seems to be popular and successful. He
has had printed a number of pasteboard books, each page of which represents twenty bricks, sold at 5 cents each.
In this manner the friends of the home expect to realize as many B cent pieces as there are bricks in the new
building. It is an entirely new plan of financiering, and it is likely to work well.
The location of the new building is at Nineteenth and Angelica streets, with a frontage of 146 feet and a depth
of 56. One of the fine features of the building is a rotunda entrance supported by columns and surmounted by a
handsome dome with a striking clock. It will have accommodations for 125 boys. The dormitories, lavatories and
lecreation halls will be fitted up in the most modern style.
Eleven years ago the Youths' Directory procured its first permanent home on Howard street, near Seven
teenth. This was -a two-story frame building, which soon proved Inadequate.
During this period of eleven years the directory has passed through Us portals 5500 boys, who have been
protected and provided for without care or cost to State or county. Of late the increase of applicants for admission
has been such as to necessitate more room. Hence the new building in a larger lot of ground.
The directory was incorporated in ISS7. The present board of directors are: The Most Rev. Archbishop, Father
D. O. Crowley, James R. Kelly. Matt I. Sullivan, Thomas R. Bannerman, Dr. J. F. Gibbon, Dr. Joseph Oliver and
T. P. Riordan. The late Joseph A. Donohoe, Alex H. Loughborough and Henry Barroilhet were also members of
the board of directors up to the time of death.
It has been mainly through the untiring zeal and capable management of Father Crowley that the directory
as a great charitable Institution has accomplished so much good for helpless and unprotected waifs. He is an en
thusiastic believer in the maxim that "prevention is better than cure." He believes It is better to spend time and
money in housing, educating and training the unprotected waifs and orphan boys of the State, to the end that they
may grow up good, law-abiding citizens, than to neglect them and allow them to become criminals. The doors of
the directory are open at all hours of the day and night to the juvenile victims of poverty and vice. It is marked
by the most broad cosmopolitanism, and has numbered among its inmates representatives of almost every people
on the face of the globe.

past year that have been briefly told in

lander's sisters was disinherited by the
terms of her father's will.
She Is Mrs. Richard Grogan Jr.
Richard Grogan is the son of the pro
prietor of the livery stable where the
horses of the Clark family were kept.
By reason of this fact Miss Clark was
occasionally called upon to enter into
conversation with the stableman's son.
She fell in love with him and they
eloped and were married. For this her
father never forgave her, a fact that
was made manifest by his omitting to
>rovidc for her in his will. The other

DEATH OF DR. STOUT.
Dr. Arthur B. Stout, one of the oldest physicians of this city, died at
St. Luke^s Hospital on last Thursday. The deceased was 84 years of age
at the time of his death. He was a native of New York, and came out to
San Francisco as surgeon of the old steamship California which was the
first steam vessel to round the Horn with passengers for the gold fields in
1549. He practiced medicine here for many years, and was widely known
among the older San Franciscans. The weight of years finally incapacitated
him. and for the past five years he has been at St. Luke's "Hospital. His
funeral will take place to-day from Pioneer Hall at 1 o'clock
Hermann Oelrichs Here.
Herman Oelrichs arrived in the city
last night on the overland from New
York. He comes on some private busi
ness matters and will remain for three
or four weeks before returning to his
home. When seen last night Mr. Oel
richs said that he knew nothing what
ever of the alleged discovery of the pa
pers in the Fair will case, and that the
first he had heard of the matter was
When he read of it in a paper he secured
at Sacramento. Mrs. Oelrichs has gone
to Europe, accompanied by Miss Fair
and her two children, and will probably
remain abroad several months. The con
dition of her eyesight has much im
proved and her husband has hopes of her
complete recovery before long. Mr. Oel
richs refused to discuss the Cuban situ
ation for publication further than to say
that, in his opinion, the matter would be
settled without a resort to arms.
Remembered the Nurses.
Mrs. Schuller, who was shot by her
husband and lay in the Harbor Hospital
for two weeks, took a pleasing method
of showing her appreciation of the care
she received at the hands of the nurses
at that Institution, yesterday, when she
appeared there with two gold medals,
which she presented to the two matrons.
On one side of each of the medals was
inscribed a sentiment of thanks and on
the other side the name of one of the
ladles who gave her the attention which
was mainly responsible tor her recovery.

The greyhounds at both Ingleside and
Union parks will enter upon a struggle
this afternoon besides which a mere
Congressional altercation wouldn't show
the heat of an Alaskan glacier. At Union
Park an all-age open stake will be run
off and with it a consolation event for
the dogs failing to successfully negotiate
theJr initial courses. At Ingleside the
feature of the card is a stake for the
hounds that have not won third money
or better during the past six months.
The running at both parks begins at the
usual hour.
Sinaloa is said to have improved much
since her appearance at Ingleside last
â week. She will soon be back in her old
stake-winning form.

tis. Cavalier will certainly be pretty
close to the top.

interstate interest.
An Eastern leashman, writing to a lo
cal publication, takes exception to a few
remarks lately made in The Call relative

bred dogs won both stakes, namely. Magic and
Coralie. The former is by Miller's liab out of
Lady Pembroke, and, I believe, was whelped
at Huron, S. D., and raised at St. Louis, Mo.
Coral by Babazoun, out of Buenretiro, was
whelped and raised in Colorado.
. Now, I presume a California greyhound is one
â whelped in California and an Eastern grey
hound is one whelped in the East.
I have the greatest respect for Californian
bred greyhounds. They breed some excellent
greyhounds, both fa.st and clever, and it takes
a rare good dog to down them, but 1 feel sure
every Californian sportsman will not object to
allow the Eastern greyhounds their dues and
what they .'airly earn.
The late Grace Cup, run for at Ingleside
Park, an Eastern dog divided first and an
other Eastern dog was third. Patrla, an East
ern greyhound, has been first or second or in
the money in all the stakes she has taken part
In and it was only a short time ago, 0:1 Feb
ruary 20, we saw grand old St. Lawrence, an
Eastern dog, who is getting too old to run
now has a crippled foot, and has been at the
stud win a fifty-four dog stake at Ingleside
I'ark and It is, perhaps, safe to say that In
his prime few If any greyhounds bred in the
East or on the Coast could lead him to the
bare.
In all this the gentleman Is undoubted
ly correct. But the article appeared in
The Call March 21. Let us look back of
that date. Of the twenty-three stakes
(covering a period of practically six
months) prior thereto Patria annexed
one and divided another. St. Lawrence
pulled down one and Diana scored one.
The other nineteen attest the worth of
coast stock, particularly as the above
named Eastern dogs were not only In the
fame often, but also several of the Van
lummell strings, several from Kay &
Train's stable, frequent representations
from Scott &â¢ Glassen's kennels, divers
of Howe it Thompson's flyers. Simmons
& Donahue's Colorado productions and
iodly number of others from the
East. That the Eastern stock has been
making a creditable showing at Ingle-
Blde lately is admitted. But the article
in The Call, when written, was certainly
not without warrant and the coa.st dogs
o cause to shirk a course with
their competitors from beyond the moun
tains.

Am the time approaches for the intercolle
giate field day, the prospect, never bright for
Stanford, grows more and more gloomy. Char
lie Dole, on whom the college relied for at least
two first places, Is In bed with a strained ten
don. Everything is being done to bring him
around. Great doubt is entertained, however,
as to his ability to compete at all. If he re
covers in time to take part, his lack of train
ing will place him at a great disadvantage.
Jack Brur.ton, also. Is not doing as well as
was expected. His limbs an- stiff from rid
ing: and lack of training while absent from
college. Ropes are entertained, however, that
another week will bring him back to his old
form.

GETTING READY FOR
THE BENCH SHOW.
The secretary of th" San Francisco Ken
nel Club has received from New York an
unofficial intimation that the suspension
of the Mastiff Club has already been can
celed, but in the absence of official con
firmation this report must be accepted
with the proverbial grain of salt. It seems
that the time is too short for any such
measure to nave been taken. The San
Francisco Kennel (Hub is naturally anx
ious for the reinstatement of the Pacific
Mastiff Club, as the latter has offered
some valuable prizes for competition at
the show.
At a meeting of the committee on
judges last evening the question of the
retention of George Bell was definitely
settled in the affirmative.
Seventy-five per cent of the profits of
the show will be devoted to the cause of
charity. Mr. Oldham, the superintendent
of tho show, will arrive here on the 27th
inst., and will :it onre take charge of the
preliminary work. Neither pains nor ex
pense will be spared to insure a success
ful show.
Applications for premium lists and en
try blanks have already been received
from New York and Now Orleans. The
premium lists will bo issued next Monday.
The Oakland bench show will open two
weeks alter the close of the San Fran
ci.sco show, and David J. Sinclair will su
perintend it. The judge has not yet been
selected, but it is a foregone conclusion
tnat the Alameda Sportsmen's Associa
tion will not reappoint their last year's
judge.
F. R. Webster will shortly break up his
splendid cocker spaniel kennels at the
Country Club, and tho fine little hunters
of which he is so proud will be scattered
far and wide.

GOOD FLY FISHING
ON COAST STREAMS.
Sonoma Creek, which Is one of the
prettiest trout streams on the line of the
San Francisco and Xorth Pacific Hail
road, will doubtless be well stocked with
trout fry this year.
Some six years ago, when the I,a Motte
hatchery was in operation near Glen El
len, trout fishing- on the creek was good
during all months of the season, but
since the stocking of the stream, which
was done by experienced hands, had
ceased the sport gradually faded away.
Some people attribute the poor fishing
of the past three or four years to the
pollution of the waters from the debris
of the asylum, which place is located
near Glen Ellen; but when fishing above
the asylum has been equally poor, then
it becomes patent that something other
than the pollution of the waters has had
something to do with the famng off of
the grand sport that was enjoyed on the
creek some years ago.
With good and intelligent stocking an
nually Sonoma Creek can be made very
popular fishing waters for local anglers.
There is, however, tolerably good sport
at present to be had on the stream. Some
nice creels of trout have been taken dur
ing the past week. Charles H. Linn of
446 California street and John Sloane
caught sixiy very nice pan fish last Sun
day, one of which weighed nearly two
pounds, and on Wednesday last A. Har
rison of Glen Ellen landed fifty trout,
many of .which measured from eight to
twelve inches. Harrison writes: "There
are plenty of fish in the creek, but they
have been slow to bite, because of the
rich food in the stream, but they have
now commenced to take fly and spoon
with avidity."
Paper Mill Creek is holding its record
as the most prolific coast stream in the
State. Good catches have been made on
it this week. The Sh^pard brothers
caught 12ri trout, a few days ago. and
among that number were fifteen fish
that weighed from half a pound to one
pound. â¢
Jim Orndorff caught some nice trout
last Tuesday in San Gregorio Creek, but
Jim's sport was spoiled after he had
taken an involuntary dip in one of the
deep pools.
Good trout fishing is reported from
Salmon Creek, nenr jjodega, and Dutch
Bill ('r.ek, tn-tween Camp MocKer and
Tyrone station, which is near Russian
River.
A striped bass weighing 25 pounds
was caught in Russian River near Dun
cans Mills last week by an angrier who
was trolling with a Wilson spoon for
steelheads.

TO BATTLE FOR
COLLEGE
CHAMPIONSHIPS.
It will take Stanford some time to re
cover from the shock its baseball men
received last week in the initial game of
the three which are to decide the cham
pionship between the two colleges. With
ten hits but three runs were scored, and
California, with five hits to its credit,
tallied seven times. This distinctly and
unerringly goes to prove what coaching
has lone for the Blue and Gold. With
a paucity of material, Cochran has
evolved a team which by its superior
knowledge of the game snatched a vic
tory when, under the natural laws of
chance, defeat should have been its por
tion.
The difference in the two college nines
this year is readily patent, even to an
unobservant spectator. Stanford has a
hitting team; California has not. Cali
fornia nas a nine of unparalleled fielders.
The same cannot be said for Stanford.
Strange to say, California plays as a team
and uoes not fall apart at critical mo
ments. Stanford needs balance and self
composure, two things which, with their
hitting abilities, wouid be a death knell
to all California's aspirations on the
diamond for this season. One hears on
â  -â¢ -i v â â â¢ i forma won on !uck last
Saturday; but the old-time professionals
and some of the later products of the
diamond who saw the game rebut
thia sin nuously. Thc-ir verdict is
that California won on its merits
and is likely to do this after
noon in the second game of the series,
unless Stanford plays much better ball
than that of a week ago.
To-day's game is the most important of
all. It means loss of the banner for
Stanford should a second defeat mar
their standards, and will probably meaji
a majority of games for them should the
Cardinal be triumphant. Beckett is a
vastly improved pitcher. He is steady,
accurate and sure, surpassing Kaarsberg
in speed and curves. During the week
he was worked hard for a few days, and
then rested. Shc^han, Stanford's coach,
was prostrated with grief on account of
defeat, but that did not prevent him from
working his men in iieid practice until
their hands were almost sore. The prac
tice has been better in form and team
work, improved upon until the red coats
are now the semblance of a team. But
for California's improvement in stick
work ami a sustention of their splend.d
field operations there is no reason why
Stanford should not win the match to
day. That the gam mbe closely fought
every indication as .vs. Devoid of acci
dents, a hot struggle s ovid be seen.
With the exception of Bride, first base
man for tho Blue and Gold, the team has
been in perfect condition physically. Bride
is suffering from a severe cold, but will
play in the gamp. The teams will line
up in tho samo order as last week, unless
changes are decided upon at a very late
hour. Following is the order.

CHAMPION RACQUET
WIELDERS AT WORK.
Tennis players are fondly waiting for
the reports of the great Ojai Valley tour
nament, probably the most Important
ever held In California, The general be
lief is that the north will be triumphant
over the south in every battle. The Whit
neys and Hardys left the city last
Wednesday evening: for the valley, and a
gathering of tennis players was at the
ferry to wish them success and victory.
Rarely has any tennis tournament caused
as much interest as this which will be
completed to-day. In the minds of those
who know a thine or two about tennis
ttfere is no doubt concerning the result
of the tournament; that the Whitney and
Hardy freres will win not only the major
ity of matches, but every one played, is
their firm belief. However, they will find
strong men oppobed to them, and they
will have to play to carry off the palms.
At the California Club some very good
matches were played during the week,
and arrangements mnde for others to
follow next week. On Monday the oft
postponed match between Miss Hoffman
and Miss Mason for the club champion
ship in singles will be played. In mixed
doubles Sumner Hardy and Miss Clark
cleared the courts with sweeping: victor
ies. Miss McLeran. a fair visitor from
the south, played several matches on tho
courts during the past week and taught
the young lady players something of the
game. With Miss Tsabelle Sherwood of
Alameda she defeated Miss Winifred
Sherwood and Miss Mann 6âl. Miss Mc-

mfle relay race indulged in by the cycling
clubs around the bay is marked by the
number of road races and "try-outs" be
ing held each Sunday.
To-morrow there will be three of these
road races, held by the Olympic, Bay
City and Imperial clubs. The Olympic
race commands the most prominence, be
cause of the number of entries and tho
fact that a "record sanction" has been
secured, in the hope that one of the rid
ers may eclipse the best previous per
formance. The race is lor live miles,
from San Leandro to Haywards, start

H. W. SPALDINU.
AN EMERGENCY ROLL.
Plan to Recruit for First Regiment,
!tT. G. C. â The New Service
Uniforms Are Here.
At a meeting of the Board of Officers of
the First Regiment of Infantry, N. G. C,
held last Thursday night, it was re
solved to open an emergency company roll
at each of the two armories. The pur
pose of this is to enable any of the ex-
National Guardsmen,' who, for various
reasons, were honorably discharged from
the service, to be ready to again become
members of any of the companies they
might desire. It is not, at this time, the
Intent to muster the men who may sign
the emergency roll, but to have them
ready at short notice should the occa
sion arise for their services.
These rolls will be opened on Monday
night at the Ellis street armory, where
those who may desire to enroll their
names with the companies that meet
there that night will have an opportun
ity to do so. The rolls will also be opened
at the Page street armory, where two
companies will meet for drill that night.
Every night next week the armories will
be open on company nights and In addi
tion there will be at each armory an of
ficer who will impart information as to
where the members of the consolidated
companies, that is, those which belong
to the regiments that were mustered out
under the plan of reorganization, can be
found, as there are, no doubt, a great
number of ex-Guardsmen who would pre
fer to be with old companions-in-arms.
Most of the service uniforms that were
ordered for the National Guard several
weeks ago have been receiwd in this
city and are now in a warehouse, and
will be ready for distribution in a short
time, as soon as a proper form of re
ceipts Is drawn up.
Park Comnissioner Austin.
Park Commissioner Joseph Austin 1s
confined to his bed suffering from a bad
attach of the grip. He complai-icd of
being ill a few days ago, but paid very
little attention to his ailment. Contrary
to the wishes of his physician, ho left h*3
home before he was thoroughly well, and
as a result he had a .relapse.- His case
was further aggravated late Wednesday
by a dangerously large abscess which
formed in his oar. and since then his con
dition has demanded constant attention
from Dr. : Overend. the specialist. . His
condition was ; somewhat -, Improved yes
terday, and hopes are entertained that he
will bo out in the course of. a few day*

ARTICLE I.
Boundaries, Rights and Liabilities.
SECTION l. The municipal corpora
tion known as the City and County of
San Francisco shall remain and con
tinue a body politic and corporate, in
name and in fact, by the name of the
City and County of San Francisco, and
by that name shall have perpetual suc
cession; may sue and defend in all
courts and places and In ail matters
and proceedings; may have an:! use a
common seal and alter the same at
pleasure; may purchase, receive, hold
and enjoy real ->nd personal property;
receive bequests, gifts and donations of
all kinds of property, In fee simple, or
in trust for charitable and other pur
poses, and do all acts necessary to
carry out th~ purposes of > uch gifts,
bequests and donations, Aith power to
manage, sell, lease or otherwise dispose
of the same in accordance with the
terms of thi- gift, bequest or trust.
Sec. 2. The boundaries of the City
and County of Can Francisco are here
by declared to be those set forth in
Section Thirty-nine Hundred and Fifty
of the Political Code of California.
Sec. 3. The City and County of San
Francisco shall continue, under this
Charter, to have, hold and enjoy all
property, rights of property, rights of
action of every nature and description
of the existing municipality and is
hereby declared to be the successor of
the same.
Sec. 4. Suits, actions and proceedings
may he brought in the name of the City
and County for the recover: of any
property, money or thinr belong
ing thereto, in law or equity, or dedi
cated to public use therein, or for the
enforcement of any rights of, or con
tracts with, the City and County,
whether made or arising or accruing
before or after the adoption of this
Charter. All existing suits, actions and
proceedings in the courts or elsewhere,
to which th^city and County is a party,
ehall continue to be carried on by or
against the City and County.
Sec. 5. No recourse shall be had
against the City and County for dam
age or loss to person or property suf
fered or sustained by reason of the de
fective condition of any sidewalk
Btreet, avenue, lane, alley, court or
placo. or by reason of the defective
condition of any sewer, or by reason of
any defective drainage, whether any of
paid defects originally existed, or
whether th*Â»y were occasioned by con
struction, excavation or embankment,
nor shall there be any recourse against
the City and County for want of re
pair of any sidewalk, street, avenue,
lane, alley, court or place or by want
of repair of any sewer; ror shall there
he any recourse against the City and
County fo*- damage to person or prop
erty suffered or sustained by reason of
nccidenton any sidewalk, street, avenue,
lane, alley, cnurt or place, or by falling
from any embankment thereon or Into
any excavation therein; but in anysuch
ca.se the person or persons on whom
the law may have imposed the obli
gation to repair such defect in the
fidewalk. street or public highway, or
fn the sewer, and also the officer or
officers through whose official negli
genre such defect remains unrepaired
chall be jointly and severally liable to
the party injured for the damage sus
tained.

prescribe.

3. Keep a Journal of its proceedings,
and allow the same to be published.
The ayes and noes shall on demand of

therein.
4. Have authority to punish its mem
bers for disorderly 6r contemptuous

12. To purchase or acquire by con

13. Except as otherwise provided in

the location and quality of all appli
ances necessary to the furnishing f

of the City and Ccunty, and for flush-
Ing the sewers therein.

ance in the month of February of each

mits from the Board of Police Com

16. To prescribe fines, forfeitures and

17. To fix the fees and charges for
all official services not otherwise pro

18. To allow not to exceed two thou
sand five hundred dollars in any year
for the celebration of the anniversary
of our National Independence, and not
to exceed five hundred dollars in any

19. To appropriate such sums as may

lected on convic on of persons charged

ize the payment of the same or some

20. To provide for the payment of
rompensat:on to the Interpreters ap
pointed by the Judges of the Superior
C urt. to interpret testimony in crim
inal cases in said Court or the Police
Court, or upon inquests and examina

each interpreter.
21. To offer rewards not exceeding
one thousand dollars In any one in
stance for the apprehension and convic
tion of any person who may have com

and County, and Seals for the several

25. To set apart as a boulevard or
boulevards any street or streets, or por

street railroad.
26. To construct or permit the con
struction of tunnels, under such rules
and regulations as the Board may pre
scribe.
27. To regulate street railroads,
tracks and cars; to compel the owners
of two or more of such roads using the
same street for any distance not ex
ceeding ten blocks to use the same
tracks and to equitably divide the cost
of construction and expense of main
tenance thereof between the owners; to
fix, establish and reduce the fares and

and goods thereon; to regulate rates of
speed, and to pass ordinances to pro
tect the public from danger or incon
venience in the operation of such roads.
28. To allow any transcontinental or
other railroad company having not less
than fifty miles of road actually con
structed id in operation to enter the
City and County with its road and run
its cars to the water front at the most
suitable point for public convenience.
No exclusive right shall be granted to
any railroad company; and the use of
all such rights shall at all times be sub
ject to regulation by the Supervisors.
Every ordinance granting such right
shall be upon the conditions that said
company shall pave and keep in repair
the street from curb to curb in such a
manner and with such material as may
from time to time be prescribed by the
Supervisors, and that such company
shall allow any other railroad company
to use in common with it the same
track or tracks, each paying an equal
portion for the construction and repair
of the tracks and appurtenances used
by such railways jointly.

30. To provide for the execution of
all trusts confided to the City and
County.
31. To transfer from one department

32. To provide for the lease of any

riod than twenty years.
33. To provide for the sale at public

Sec. 2. The Supervisors shall consti
tute the Board of Equalization of the
City and County. The Clerk of the Su
pervisors shall be Clerk of the Board of
Equalization by virtue of his office.
Sec. 3. The Board of Supervisors
shall appoint from its members a com
mittee consisting of three to be denom
inated Finance Committee, and shall
fill all vacancies in the Committee.
The Committee shall investigate the
transactions and accounts of all officers
having the collection, custody or dis
bursement of public money, or having
the power to approve, allow, or audit
demands on the treasury; shall have
free access to any records, books and
papers in all public offices; shall have
power to administer oaths and affirma
tions, and to examine witnesses, and
compel their attendance before them by
subpena. The Committee may at any
time visit any of the public offices and
make its examinations and investiga
tions therein without hindrance.
The Committee must, at least once In
every six months, examine the official
bonds of all City and County officers,
and investigate the sufficiency and sol
vency of the sureties thereon, and re
port in writing the facts to the Mayor.
Such report shall specify each bond
with the sureties, and the amounts for
which each surety is bound, and state
whether or not they are sufficient and
solvent. Upon such report the Mayor
shall take such action as shall be nec
essary to protect the City and County,
and may require new bonds when nec
essary, and he may suspend any officer
till a sufficient bond Is filed and ap
proved.
Sec. 4. The Finance Committee shall
have power, and it shall be its duty, to
examine the records and examine and
expert the books of account of all per
sons, companies or corporations that
are required to pay a portion of their
gross receipts into the treasury; and
shall likewise, as an aid to the fixing
of rates for furnishing water and light
to the City and County and to the in
habitants thereof, have like power, and
it shall be its duty, to examine the
records and examine and expert the
books of ac ount of any and all per
sons, companies or corporations so
furnishing water or light.
In the exercise of its functions, the
concurrence of two members of the
Committee shall be deemed sufficient.
The Committee shall keep a record of
its proceedings with the names of the
witnesses examined and a substantial
statement of the evidence taken. If.
from the examination made by the
Committee, it shall appear thnt a mis
demeanor in office, or a defalcation,
has been committed by an officer, the
Committee shall immediately report to
the Mayor, who, if he approve the re
port, shall take such proceedings
against such officer as are authorized
by law, and may suspend him pending
such proceedings. Any Police Officer
execute the process and orders of
the Committee.
Sec. 5. No exclusive franchise or
privilege shall be granted for laying
pipes, wires or conduits.
Sec. 6. The Board of Supervisors
shall have power to grant authority
for a term not exceeding twenty-five
years to construct and operate street
railways upon, or over, or under, the
streets or parts of streets of the City
and County not reserved for boulevards
or carriage driveways, upon the follow
ing conditions and in the following
manner and none other:
Upon application being made to the
Board for any such franchise, it shall
by resolution determine whether such
franchise or any part thereof should
be granted, and at said time shall de
termine on what conditions the same
shall be granted additional to those
conditions provided in this Chapter.
After such determination, it shall
cause notice of such application and
resolution to be advertised in the offi
cial newspaper of the City and Coun
ty for ten consecutive days. Such ad
vertisement must be completed not less
than twenty nor more than thirty days
before a*iy further action is taken by
the Board on such application. The ad
vertisement must state the character
of the franchise sought, the term of
Its proposed continuance, and the
route to be traversed; that sealed bids
will be received up to a certain hour
on a day to be named in the advertise
ment; and a further statement that
no bids will be received of a stated
amount, but that all bids must be for
the payment to the City and County
in lawful money of the United States
of a stated percentage of the gross
annual receipts of the person, com
pany or corporation to whom the fran
chise may be awarded, arising from its
use. operation, enjoyment or posses
sion.
Every bidder shall file with his bid a
bond executed to tfie City and County,
with at least two good and sufficient
Buretles to be approved by the Mayor
in a penal sum prescribed by the Su
pervisors, and set forth in such ad
vertisement, conditioned that such bid
der will well and truly observe, fulfill
and perform each and all cf the condi
tions, terms and obligations of the
franchise for which said application
was made in case The same shall be
awarded to him, and that in case of
the breach of any of the conditions of
such bond, the whole amount of the
penal sum therein named shall be taken
to be liquidated damages, and that as
such shall be recoverable from the
principal and sureties on such bond.
At the next regular session after the
expiration of the time stated in such
advertisement up to which such bids
will be received, the Board must open
such bids _nd award the franchise to
the person, company or corporation of
fering to pay the highest stated per
centage of the gross receipts arising
from the use, operation, possession or
enjoyment of the franchise for which
such application was made. But no
award shall be made, nor any such ap
plication granted, unless the stated
percentage offered to be paid for the
franchise shall be at least three per
centum of such gross receipts during
the first five years of the period for
which the franchise is to be granted,
four per centum of the gross receipts
during the next succeeding ten years,
and five per centum of the gross re
ceipts during the next succeeding ten
years.
Except as In this section otherwise
provided, bidding for such franchises
must t- In accordance wi h the provis
ions of this Charter In relation to bids
made to the Board of P Mic Works, so
far as such provisions may be applica
ble. The Supervisors -.iay reject any
and all bids, and may refuse to grant a
franchise for any part of tr* 1 route for
which application was made. "! cry
ordinance making such grant shall re
quire the concurrenceof three-fourthsof
all the members of the Board of Super
visors, as shown by the ayes and noes,
and the approval of the May
or, and at least ninety days shall in
tervene between the introduction and
final passage of any such ordinance. It
shall require a vote of five-sixths of all
the Supervisors to pass the ordinance
notwithstanding the objections of the
Mayor.
If any bid be accepted, the franchise
must be granted upon the express con
dition, in addition to the conditions re
quired by this Charter, and such other
conditions as may be prescribed by the
Supervisors, that the per centum of the
gross receipts of the railway shall be
paid into the treasury on or before the
tenth day of the next ensuing month
after such gross receipts shall have
been earned; and upon the further con
dition that the whole of the railway
shall be continuously operated, and
that at the end of the term the road
track and bed of such railway and all
its stationary fixtures upon the public
streets, shall become the property of
the City and County; and that the
grantees will, within one hundred days
after the date of such grant, commence
the construction of such railway, and
continuously thereafter, in each and ev
ery month until the completion thereof,
expend in such construction at least
the sum of three thousand dollars.
The failure to comply with any of
said conditions shall work an immedi
ate forfeiture of such franchise and the
road or track constructed thereunder.
There shall be no power In the Super
visors to relieve from such forfeiture
or from any of said conditions. On or
before the tenth day of each month af
ter said receipts shall have been earned,
the President and Secretary of said
railway company shall make and file
with the Clerk of. the Board of Super
visors a sworn statement of the gross
receipts of such railway for the pre
ceding month.
In granting any such franchise the '
Board of Supervisors shall impose such
other lawful conditions as it may deem
advisable, and must expressly provide I
that the franchise shall not be renewed
or regranted. and that the Board shall
at all time's have the power to regulate
the rates of fare to be charged by those
using, operating, possessing or enjoy
ing the franchise, and that the Finance
Committee of the Board shall at all
times be permitted to examine and ex
pert their books as to such gross re
ceipts. All moneys received for such
franchises and in payment of the said
per centum shall be credited to the
General Fund.
Sec. 7. The Supervisors shall have no
power to grant franchises or privileges
to erect poles or wires for transmitting
electric power or for lighting purposes
along or upon any public street or high
way of the City and County except up
on all the conditions and in the manner,
including competitive bidding and pay
ment of a percentage of gross receipts,
hereinbefore set out, and upon the fur
ther condition that the Board shall at
all times have the right to regulate the
charges of any person, company or cor
poration using, enjoying or possessing
such franchise or privilege.
When, on the expiration of any street
railroad franchise, it shall be deemed
inexpedient by the Board to use any of
the property reverting to it by reason
of such expiration in the operation of
a street railroad, then the Board shall
have power to lease such property to
any person, company or corporation af
ter the notice, on the terms, and in the
manner above provided as to the grant
ing of street railroad .ranchises, as far
as the same may be applicable. But no
ordinance uthorizing such lease shall
be passed prior to ninety days next pre
ceding the expiration of such franchise.
Any ordinance granting a franchise
or authorizing a lease under the provis
ions of this section shall be in force
from and after the expiration of thirty
days from the date of its signature by j
the Mayor, or from and after the expi
ration of thirty days from the date of
Its passage by the Supervisors over his
objections, unless within said thirty
days a petition signed by a number of â 
the electors of the City and County j
equal to fifteen per centum of the votes
cast at the last preceding election shall
have been filed with the Supervisors,
asking that said ordinance be submit
ted to the vote of the people. In such
case said ordinance shall be submitted
at the next election to the vote of the
electors of the City and County.' and
unless said ordinance shall at said elec
tion receive in its favor a majority of
the votes cast thereon it shall have no
force or effect for any purpose. If a j
majority of the votes be in favor of
such ordinance, the Board of Election ' :
Commissioners shall, on the conclusion
of the canvass of the vote thereon,
proclaim such fact, and upon such
proclamation said ordinance shall have
full force and effect as of the date i
aforesaid. Said petition and submission
shall be made In accordance with the
provisions of section twenty of Chapter
I of this Article.
Sec. 8. All claims for damages
against the City and County must be
presented to the Board of Supervisors i
and filed with the Clerk within six
months after the occurrence from '
which the damages are claimed to have
arisen; otherwise there shall be no re- ;

Sec. 11. On or before the last Mon

for City and County purposes required
to be levied upon all property not ex

upon the treasury' authorised to be paid

sive of the State tax and the tax to pay
the interest and maintain the sinking
funds of the bonded Indebtedness of the

tax to pay for the maintenance and

public grounds of the City and County,
shall not exceed the rate of one dollar
on each one hundred dollars" valuation
of the property assessed. The Super

tion the taxes to the several funds.
Sec. 12. In making the apportion
